SENTPOS COCA_acad_wlp_2009_06_FILE##4079805 COCA  A    0   94 In addition , many of these studies have sought to trace the complicated and shifting relationship between the dominant class , mostly wealthy and identified as " white " which recognized and the religion , most of whom were of lower socio-economic status and identified as " black " or " African " n15 After the abolition of slavery in 1888 and until the 1930s , the state of Bahia repressed the practice of Candombl by outlawing ceremonies , confiscating sacred objects that are central to the religion , and ordering the arrest of individuals who were caught in possession of its material culture ( Butler 1998 , Graden 2006 , Reis 1993 , Sansi 2007 ) .

SENTPOS COCA_acad_wlp_2009_06_FILE##4079805 COCA  A    0  137 CANDOMBL ALTARS IN SACRED SPACES Ax , the powerful force that drives the universe , holds a central position in the practice of Candombl .

SENTPOS COCA_acad_wlp_2009_06_FILE##4079805 COCA  A    0  239 AESTHETIC SHIFTS IN PUBLIC ART The creation of public art projects depicting Candombl , such as the orix sculptures by Tatti Moreno , necessitates a fundamental shift in aesthetics , function , and meaning as sacred symbols are removed from the context of the terreiro and reinterpreted for a broad audience .
SENTPOS COCA_acad_wlp_2009_06_FILE##4079805 COCA  B    0  239 AESTHETIC_JJ SHIFTS_NN2 IN_II PUBLIC_JJ ART_NN1 The_AT creation_NN1 of_IO public_JJ_NN1 art_NN1 projects_NN2 depicting_VVG Candombl_NP1_NN1 ,_Y such_II21 as_II22 the_AT orix_NN1 sculptures_NN2 by_II Tatti_NP1_JJ Moreno_NP1_NN1 ,_Y necessitates_VVZ a_AT1 fundamental_JJ shift_NN1@_VV0 in_II aesthetics_NN1 ,_Y function_NN1_VV0@ ,_Y and_CC meaning_VVG_NN1 as_RG@_CSA_II@ sacred_JJ symbols_NN2 are_VBR removed_VVN from_II the_AT context_NN1 of_IO the_AT terreiro_NN1_JJ and_CC reinterpreted_VVD for_IF a_AT1 broad_JJ audience_NN1 ._Y
SENTPOS COCA_acad_wlp_2009_06_FILE##4079805 COCA  A    0  240 The members of this audience come from diverse cultural and religious backgrounds , and individuals in this varied population interpret , representations in a public context are intended to be seen as art works , not as ritual objects .
SENTPOS COCA_acad_wlp_2009_06_FILE##4079805 COCA  B    0  240 The_AT members_NN2 of_IO this_DD1 audience_NN1 come_VVN@_VV0 from_II diverse_JJ cultural_JJ and_CC religious_JJ backgrounds_NN2 ,_Y and_CC individuals_NN2 in_II this_DD1 varied_JJ population_NN1 interpret_VV0 ,_Y representations_NN2 in_II a_AT1 public_JJ_NN1 context_NN1 are_VBR intended_VVN to_TO be_VBI seen_VVN as_CSA_II@ art_NN1 works_VVZ_NN ,_Y not_XX as_RG@ ritual_JJ objects_NN2 ._Y
SENTPOS COCA_acad_wlp_2009_06_FILE##4079805 COCA  A    0  241 Therefore , the element of empowerment , so important within the sacred context of the terreiro , is eliminated in public art. n39 Specifically , recall that Moreno 's images on the Dique are figurative representations of people who have incorporated the orixs in trance , and they are depicted as they would appear in a Candombl ceremony .

SENTPOS COCA_acad_wlp_2009_06_FILE##4079805 COCA  A    0  299 As Sansi has observed , the failure of the Pentecostal protestors in Bahia to change the course of the commission indicates that at that particular historical moment , the Pentecostal movement , and specifically the Igreja Universal do such as Rio de Janeiro , did not have enough political leverage to counter the strong cultural politics of Bahia ( ibid. , p. 172 ) .

SENTPOS COCA_acad_wlp_2009_06_FILE##4079805 COCA  A    0  300 When the Pentecostal community originally protested these works , they attributed power to them , arguing that they would unleash a negative force in the city and could even cause physical illness to viewers .
